The leviathan has a tailfin that moves up and down, which is classic in aquatic mammals. Whales, dolphins, otters, seals, etc., all have tails that go up and down, because they once had hips and knees. They don't consider you prey. Even small children aren't recognized as prey as their size isn't a determining factor in what sharks want to eat. Simply put; we don't smell like food to sharks.  Most shark attacks seem to be an expression of territory enforcement or annoyance and happen in deeper water (near the surface in at least 20 meters). BUT there have been a couple of known cases, like the school kid that jumped off some sort of tourism vessel about 5 years ago. No one is sure what happened (it was at night with very poor lighting), but it does appear to be a case of shark attack. Couple of things about that though: the sharks follow the boat as they've learned that tourists will throw food in the water, and this was deeper water a few hundred meters offshore, but in about 30 meter deep water in known Tiger shark territory (there are a few sharks that are more aggressive already, like Tiger sharks).  Just a series of least optimal conditions mixed with one really bad decision. Don't be stupid and you'll be fine.

Theres some information in the first two minutes that I‚Äôd like to clarify.   First, ringwoodite was discovered in 2014 and a deep later of it was discovered some time later, but samples of it are extremely rare and difficult to obtain. One sample was found in Brazil and contained water in a fourth state of matter (not liquid, gas, or solid), a kind of molecular crystal.   Based on that sample and some synthetic ringwoodite that researchers have created in perfect laboratory conditions, it is THEORISED to be capable of holding 3x the water in the oceans, but there is no way to currently prove that it does contain that much right now, and no guarantee that it all holds as much molecular water as was found in that one sample.   Second, we can determine what oil and other fossil fuels came from by analysing the fossil record of where the oil was extracted. Oil, coal and natural gas are the results of dead plants AND animals from millions of years ago, and that does include BOTH marine plants and animals, and dinosaurs. It is not a myth that fossil fuels come from dinosaurs, just that ALL fossil fuels come from dinosaurs.   No shade to you Roanoke, I love your vids I just feel like with how much everything is being questioned in the world lately, its important to be accurate and accountable when we can. Much love.   Sources:   https://theticker.org/14058/science/body-of-ringwoodite-water-found-under-earths-surface/#:~:text=Northwestern%20geophysicist%20Steve%20Jacobsen%20has,our%20oceans%20combined%20three%2Dfold.  https://ocean.si.edu/conservation/gulf-oil-spill/what-are-fossil-fuels#:~:text=Fossil%20fuels%20are%20compound%20mixtures,and%20the%20amount%20of%20pressure.

That girl feeling "high" has nothing to do with oxygen (too much or too little). It has everything to do with nitrogen. AKA nitrogen narcosis. At greater depths you can breath an oxygen/helium mix to mitigate this. But at even greater depths, even helium becomes toxic. Either way, it's not the oxygen's fault, it's the other gasses fault.

Talking about how theres features youd change because things dont make sense or arent safe....most industrial accidents are because companies didnt do common sense checking before making something standard. The Byford Dolphin Incident is a famous one. A less known one that always comes to mind for me, is when a man was incinerated (alive) in a giant industrial oven used for hardening plastic canoes, because there was no way to open the door from the inside of this room sized oven if it accidentally closed on someone without anyone to witness. After the man was killed, the manufacturer of the ovens added an escape hatch, warning lights about opening and closing doors, and a way to open the main door from the inside.  Also, a lot of radiological incidents (such as facilities that use radiation to sterilize equipment) happen because installers never think "maybe we should add thick enough walls, doors, lights to indicate open doors, intercoms inside the rooms, and safety features what will prevent radiation from being emitted if the doors are open."  And then people die and international investigators find out, THEN safety features are added.

Those are Scaphander suits... suits like that for extremely deep dives (where scuba gear no longer suffices even with special air mixtures) exist even today, although the real life ones are far less mobile and look less like power armor from Halo and more like a tiny submarine with arms and legs and a helmet dome on top. They are so heavily armoured because they are designed to keep close to normal surface pressure even while this deep in the ocean. Therefore, the user inside would neither suffer from "oxygen poisoning" when the pressure gets too high nor have to ascend slowly to avoid the bends/diver's palsy. Scaphander suits are little tiny submarines.
A marine creature having "hands" is not that bizarre as Roanoke seems to think. Just look at mud-skippers (amphibiously living fish in mangrove swamps that can absorb oxygen even out of water through their wet skin and by gulping air). All vertebra animals have limbs and phalanges (even snakes have them, technically, during embryonal development, their limbs just atrophy). In fish, these turned into fins. In reptiles and most mammals, these turned into arms and legs, hands/front paws and feet, fingers and toes (except hoofed animals where the toes fused to form hooves). A fish's front fins still contain radii that are the equivalent of finger bones.  In whales (mammals that evolved on land and then returned to the oceans and adapted to aquatic lifestyle), the bones or what used to be hands and feet are still inside their fleshy flippers, providing stability.  Since the _Underwater_ creatures are clearly vertebrates, what is bizarre are the tentacles, not the "hands".
The suit itself contains air, as do the pressurised air tanks. Once the helmet cracks, water floods in, the air inside the suit blows out, and if the air tanks somehow get breached the rapidly expanding volume of air would create an even larger explosion. Not that hard to understand?
Quick note about Ringwoodite. Discovered in 1969 from a meteorite. Also, can hold water in the form of hydroxide inside of its crystal structure at the Mantle Transition Zone.

Medical/Organic Chemist here. Concerning the idea of oxygen taking 80 years to poison us, isn't actually too far off what it actually does to us. Due to the bodies use of Reacrive Oxygen Species (ROS), such as hydrogen peroxide, hydroxyl, superoxide, singlet oxygen etc. ROS all have a radical oxygen which while for the most part being extremely useful as the are biochemically more active over time these radicals cause oxidative stress, which accumulates overtime causing damage to protein, lipids, DNA etc. This accumulated damage is currently thought to be one of the leading causes of aging, which if true does mean that oxygen does poison us over time leading to death at ~80 years.

13:35 - The brain to body mass ratio, also known as cephalic index, is a weird rough estimate that works well not only to measure potential intelligence/cognitive capacities of a species, but also its development throughout maturation.   The weird part is that for humans, that ratio is somewhere 1.2-1.1 of the optimum, making our brain mass unnecessarily large, even for evolutionary adaptations. The cool part is that nobody knows why such ratio happened in our species (chimpanzees are a runner-up here) since callosotomy patients and even people who went through hemispherectomy can retain impressive amount of cognitive functions. Boyles law.   Gases in you body become compressed at depth, even in a pressure suit. This is why deep divers have 3phase tanks to include helium, and will take decompression stops while coming back to the surface.   Going from these depths to roughly 1 atmosphere pressures inside of a seconds, would result in the gasses in your body, occupying approximately 40-50x the amount of volume/space in your body as they did at depth. . .   Hence bologna mist o'matic

Hey Roanoke, got the answer for you about the pressure explosions! While they're a bit oversold in the movie, what you're seeing is a cavitation bubble. The pressure is so great that the crushed air pocket is superheated in a microsecond, with the massive spike in thermal energy flash boiling a chunk of water. It's the same trick that mantis shrimp use!

Very good watch. However, onto the mystical nature of Cthulhu and the mythos known as the Cthulhu Mythos (where Cthulhu plays only a minor role, as it is absolutely not a deity), Cthulhu, despite being describe as a paranormal entity, would technically be only a member of an alien specie, and mentionned only because it is considered in their own texts as the Highpriest of his own race. Cults can be formed only due to members of the same race as Cthulhu being able to transcend most of human perceptions and boundaries and their evolution on different planes of existence. However, their bodies, in corporeal forms, have the weakness of any flesh, excepting the extraordinary nature of their abilities: shrinking to neigh human size, whilst their size could go up to a hundreds of meters high, and temporary dispersion, as showcased in the novel titled "The Call of Cthulhu", when a steamboat on the raging sea crashes into the eldritch creature, and ending up on the other side of it.  However as much as these would seem paranormal, considering the nature of spatial overdimension, or perhaps better said as the property of having unknown and varying spatial dimensionnal status of the architecture of R'lyeh, the only city of the Old Ones, it is safe to say that their abilities are not as much abilities as natural capacities inherent to creatures who have been evolving into 8, 9 or who knows how many dimensions of space.  An interesting concept to view these creatures would be to imagine us facing an animal without capacity to evolve out of an X grid, for it has all its existence lived into a line, or has never been able to develop senses enough or the organs to evolve into more than 2 dimensions, 3 if we account for time of course.  Interestingly enough, many speak of Cthulhu's children, however, despite his followers sometimes refered as such, the old ones have never been stated throughout lovecraft's work to be able to copulate with humans, like the Deep Ones, (the fish people) can. As a matter of fact, the Deep Ones, linked to their two founders Dagon and Hydra, could be a lot closer to the species seen in Underwater as could be thought !  For anyone unfamiliar with the Deep Ones, a few things are to be known. They are a specie often misjudged to have ties with Cthulhu, however only a few novels of the 3rd to 4th lovecraftean cycle give nudges into that direction, whereas Lovecraft himself in different novels stated that they stem from two ancestors, who are revered as living gods, Dagon and Hydra.  Deep ones are described as livid, repulsive looking and deformed, however, in their own right, they are immortal beings and live in what seems to be a pretty cool utopia under the seas. They deal with humans in what is however a rather unethiqual way, as they use them in a somewhat parasitic way, even if some would call it closer to a symbiotic relationship, they provide good fortune with their fishing, and they get to procreate, for they are unable to procreate amongst themselves, which could be a direct link to the hormones inducing their own immortality.  Seeing as they can live through centuries and how marine life tends to get bigger the deeper, and that some life forms can grow across the full of their lifespan, it could be possible that Dagon and Hydra are merely just overly old and senile Deep Ones, not all that different to the others and not gods at all, even tho an encounter with such depraved, unsightly and massive creatures would be dangerous, they are not aliens to this plane of existence, and to earth, and would fit this theory of diving lifeforms turning  over isolation and century, plus inbreeding here, into a very different breed of animal, being a far far cousin to humans.   I may ask something a bit unorthodox, but could you possibly make a video on something that I feel could be interesting, that is to say, different creatures who biologically can survive space vacuum, live in space, or move in space. Even not regarding lovecraft's work (with Blaakis, Mi'gos and Ancient Ones being able to physically withstand the void) there are plenty of medias who depict such creatures, and it would be interesting to dwell on the possibility of extra planetary lifeforms and organisms.

Imagine if there were a sequel to this movie, but it was a TV series about Liam and Emily, the only survivors. And if this was the script:  "In the aftermath of the deep-sea disaster, Liam and Emily find themselves burdened with survivor's guilt. As the only survivors, they feel a profound sense of responsibility towards their fallen coworkers and friends who lost their lives in the tragedy. To their dismay, Tian Industries, the deep-sea drilling corporation they once trusted, shows little remorse and takes no responsibility for the lives lost.  This callous disregard for the lives of their coworkers becomes a driving force behind Liam and Emily's determination to seek justice and bring Tian to its knees. Fueling their war against the corporation is not only their desire for personal retribution but also their deep-seated empathy for the lost souls who can no longer fight for themselves.  As they delve deeper into their investigation, Liam and Emily uncover a network of deceit, cover-ups, and corporate greed. Tian's actions are revealed to be not only criminally negligent but also intertwined with a sinister cult known as the "Cult of Cthulhu." The revelation that Tian was not only aware of the existence of ancient Eldritch abominations but actively conspired with a cult to awaken the malevolent Cthulhu sends shockwaves through Liam and Emily's world.  They soon realize that their nightmares, which have plagued them ever since the deep-sea disaster, were not just random terrors but a direct result of Cthulhu's influence seeping into their minds. The realization that their nightmares were a forewarning of the impending doom and a connection to the ancient entity adds a chilling layer of terror to their journey.  Armed with this understanding, Liam and Emily must confront not only the external threats posed by Tian and the cult but also the internal battles with their own sanity. The boundary between dreams and reality blurs as they face hallucinations, psychological torment, and the constant presence of Cthulhu within their minds. Their nightmares become both a curse and a guide, propelling them forward even as they struggle to maintain their grip on reality.  Driven by their newfound knowledge, Liam and Emily become consumed by their mission to expose both Tian and the Cult of Cthulhu. Their pursuit of justice takes them to dark and foreboding corners of the world, as they unearth ancient artifacts and decipher cryptic texts in their quest to dismantle the cult's plans and prevent the true cataclysmic awakening of Cthulhu.  As they navigate this treacherous journey, Liam and Emily's mental and emotional fortitude is tested to the limits. Nightmares and hallucinations haunt their every step, blurring the line between reality and madness. The weight of their guilt and the horrors they witness threaten to push them over the edge, but their determination to honor the memory of the fallen and thwart the cult's malevolent agenda keeps them fighting. Scuba instructor, clearing up some misconceptions: Oxygen toxicity effect isn't narcotic, if you suffer from it you'll convulse, first with your body going rigid, then more like a grand mal seizure. What is narcotic however is nitrogen, when breathing air at higher pressure you can suffer from nitrogen narcosis. CO2 is also narcotic at pressure. Which brings me to the next misconception: a deep sea hardshell suit like this wouldn't have an oxygen scrubber, it would have a CO2 scrubber, removing the CO2 from your exhaled air, so it only has to replace the oxygen you've used, oxygen tanks and CO2 scrubber is much more space and weight efficient than air tanks. CO2 also triggers the breathing response, so a bad scrubber would have you both high, and breathing heavily, trying to expell CO2 from your body.  Movie fridge logic misses: When the facility is leaking and no longer holding the water out, pressure would increase sharply inside, everyone would be getting quite high and pretty soon convulse, there wouldn't be much time, that deep, and getting into the suits would just seal that same pressure in. The whole team would be tripping and convulsing before long. That's if they even get to their suits, at that depth the pressure of the water seeping in would be like industrial waterjet cutters, it wouldn't be flowing down the walls, it would be cutting them to pieces, a pinhole opening would be like a bandsaw.

A diving suit like this is not over pressurized, it has normal human-friendly pressure and is built to resist the positive pressure difference coming from being deep undersea, so if the suit fails "pressure goes in", not out. That's why they're called atmospheric diving suits, you take a bit of ground level pressure with you in a way.

The suit imploding makes sense at such depths. When the pressure escapes, the depths makes it constrict from the largest chamber, which would be the torso/abdomen area. The sudden compression creates an outward explosive force once it ruptures.  Implosions are an inward force (like suction) that creates an outward force from the intensity of the inward force being too much for the material to stand, rupturing and releasing the compression outwards, 90 percent of the time being at a highly explosive tendency.  Many think of implosions as explosions that fo in, then release outward, which that is a possible form of implosions, but the most common implosions are from a suction to compression causing an outward burst from the incapability of the material to hold such compressive tension so suddenly.

Man, usually your stuff is solid because you stick to biology but this was hard to watch with the suits and pressure differentials.  Wait, pressure in the suit would be biology...  If the suit was pressurized to resist the inward pressure of the ocean your body would be under basically pressure equal to the water at the bottom of the ocean.  You would suffer nitrogen narcosis and die pretty damn quickly.  Even with Heliox or Hydreliox gas with a less than 1% level of oxygen you are at your PO2 limit of 1.6 at something like 1000 ft.  To be miles down there is no known and probably no possible gas combination that could prevent you from dying.  If they ahd it they wouldn't need the suits to resist the pressure then.  The suits can only work if they use mostly ambient internal pressures and then just physically resist the compression of the pressure.  The US Navy has a suit they use for diving down to like 2000+ ft and it's called the 1 atmo suit.  Because internally your body is at 1 atmosphere of pressure or 14ish psi.  You require zero decompression then but the suits are much less maneuverable than these are.   Secondly, the implosion absolutely would create an outward force.  Basically the heat caused by the compression of the air in the suit would cause water to boil off and expand.  It's why if you look at people blowing up fireworks underwater it can break the entire fish tank or in slow mo you see the cavitation and collapse over and over in a cycle until the energy dissipates.  Implosion is slightly different in the action since it's an inward rush of water without the initial outward push but imagine that the suit is the space made by an explosion and now it's closing in on it.  It will rebound and since water can't really compress it will transfer 99% or more of the energy with little to no loss.  It's more complicated than this as cavitation is also caused by local low pressure (like vacuum low) points causing the water to turn into a vapor but it instantly compresses back into water when out of the low pressure zone.  Heat and vacuum both boil water since boiling and freezing is just a combination of pressure and temperature.  They achieve the same end result mostly in the macro sense.  Source, EOD, then metrologist, and diver.

Also, props for the base imploding after being breached, which is totally what happens because the pressure is just so hilariously high it just rips everything apart. Also, props for the not being able to ascend part without specialized equipment. Thats too what happens in reality, you cannot overcome the "weight" of the water on top of you by using the normal means of air filled vessels. You need specialized buoyancy devices like tanks filled with some type of oil or a specialized foam made from glass bubbles immersed in resin, that don't get crushed by the pressure or need a vessel so thick walled it negates the buoyancy.   Minus points for the leaks in the tunnel, you cannot have leaks because the tunnel would immediately fill up with water nearly completely, because the whole volume of air gets compressed in an extremely small volume and then dissolve into the water in short order. And you cannot have over pressure high enough to stop this, because the air would literally become toxic to us at those pressures, and disrupt bodily functions.

In the Cthulhu mythos, there is a race that worships Cthulhu known as the star-spawn, or Xothians.  They resemble Cthulhu in appearance, but they're much smaller and far less powerful. There's also Dagon and his race of Deep Ones.  Not sure why you think a Lovecraftian origin would be boring, though.  None of the "gods" of the Cthulhu mythos were actually gods, nor were they truly supernatural.  They were just powerful, interdimensional beings that seemed like gods to primitive man.  Also, there's a way in biology to tell if a creature is of a truly aquatic origin or possibly mammalian origin-- look at the orientation of the spine and tail.  If it moves up and down in motion, it was likely originally a land-dwelling mammalian creature, side to side and it is of fish or reptilian origin and probably evolved entirely in an aquatic environment.  Whether the creators of this movie knew any of that or not, who knows.

16:18 the more I look at his death scene, the less sense it starts making to me. First of all, I don't think his head was ripped off. More likely it exploded, probably from being forcefully pulled into the chest area of the suit, which was fully tightened at that time (couldn't be the pressure, because they weren't outside).  Then the way his head just squashed like Play-Doh moment before he died. Would that really happen if a person was being pulled on his lower body with a lot of strength? The way his face caved in would more likely happen if something heavy hit him in the face, or if he was being sucked with a lot of strength by something. Although, granted, I think his head looked like that simply because they used a very realistic rubber head for filming, so it just behaved like rubber would. The underwater angle of his death shows us that the monster was pulling only on one of his legs. Meaning, the rest of his body was more or less left in place, so that shouldn't have caused his head to be pulled into the suit and explode. He technically should have survived. At the very least he shouldn't have immediately died. Nitrogen narcosis is the more likely cause of the "high" than high oxygen levels. While nitrogen is usually inert in the body, that is at 'normal' pressures. At depths like this nitrogen dissolves in blood and at extreme saturation behaves like a narcotic. Deep divers use mixed gasses like helium/oxygen blends, but if they don't sound like chipmunks, that's not what they are doing here. PADI-certified diver for over 35 years.

"Founded in 1643, Innsmouth was noted for ship-building before the American Revolution, after which the civic centre shifted to the present Town Square. It reached its peak as a naval hub after the War of 1812, when many of its privateering sailors were killed. As a result, there was a dip in trade for both the shipping families and local mills.  In 1846, Captain Marsh and 32 fellow cultists were arrested by Selectman Mowry. However, before they could be charged, the Deep Ones stormed the town, breaking them out and purging the resistant population. Half of the population were killed in what was covered up as a plague from China.  After the American Civil War, the last big ships stopped docking in the harbour.  It became something of an industrial centre at one point, but by the 1920s, only the Marsh Refining Company gold mill is still in operation.  After Robert Olmstead escaped Innsmouth on July 16, 1927, and reported the going-ons to authorities, a large force of federal agents laid siege to the town throughout the winter of 1927-28, demolishing most of its seafront buildings. It was later reported in February 1928 as a Prohibition-related clash, though no captives ever showed up in the prison system. It included several arrests of members of the Esoteric Order of Dagon and at least one torpedo fired into Devil's Reef. "

I'm a geologist, and to answer your question about how we know oil comes from plants and not dinosaurs:  We know that organic material needs a calm, steady environment to be eventually covered by sediment and essentially cooked into oil over millions of years. That calm, steady environment can be found in lakes, deep seas, and swamps. Because lots of plant and plant impression fossils have been found in association with oil deposits, and because animals just simply don't have enough biomass to produce the vast amounts of hydrocarbons found on the planet, we can conclude with moderate confidence that a lot of oil comes from the settling and burying of the organic material from densely vegetated swamps.  (rambling about geology over, love your content dude, keep it up!)

There is a problem with your "larger body retains heat better" while true, specifically a large BODY.  Long appendages will do the exact opposite. We see these have very long appendages so there goes that, minus the giant one.
William Eubanks (The creator) confirmed that the creature in the film is Cthulhu and the smaller humanoid predators were a product of Cthulhu. The film left out whether this version of Cthulhu was of a supernatural origin for mystery.  If this version isn't supernatural, then the other explanations could be extra-terrestrial or an ancient species with extreme adaptive capabilities and Cthulhu is the alpha of the species. If he is supernatural, then that means that the protagonist's sacrifice was in vain because Cthulhu can regenerate and is immortal. At the end of the film, it was revealed that the company was going to continue drilling in the Mariana Trench - which leaves the audience to believe that this version of Cthulu survived somehow... The humanoid creatures could either be offspring of Cthuhu and the offspring continued reproducing with each other - OR they were once human, who began to mutate due to unknown intervention by Cthulhu and were sealed off underwater due to a major planetary shift.. Its plausible that this version isn't supernatural due to what we know about H.P. Lovecraft's descriptions of him. Cthulhu resides in a realm that is essentially a pocket dimension and is summoned by ritual through his followers. Cthulhu's can project himself via telepathy, matter manipulation and he grants his loyal followers special abilities. Those who gaze upon him instantly go into madness. None of the characters who saw him in the movie fell under such influence. In Lovecraft's universe, his human disciples begin to mutate into amphibious humanoid creatures and move under water, The creatures in the film could be a result of that, or once again could be ancient or extraterrestrial race... Basically it's up in the air.

ANGLERFISH!!!
I'm torn on what this thing actually is, no doubt it took heavy inspiration of Lovecraft. But as to it being an actual cosmic horror deity, there are a few things that if falls short on. The idea that it's a natural evolution seems plausible up to a point. The underwater ape theory is intriguing and does play into some of the adaptations these creatures went through. So not much go on there, but going on to the Lovecraft angle I think there are a few ways its being used and/or being portrayed.  To explain being used, people tend to fall back on simplifying certain things or comparing them with something they are familiar with and adapting what they know and comparing it to what is going on and learning the fundamentals of how it works and how to possibly deal with it. Take for example Stranger Things, some minor spoilers, the kids in that series tended to compare the creatures they encountered to D&D creatures and/or beings to set a baseline on how they might operate. These weren't exact match ups, but still provided a baseline of okay this creature in D&D acted like this creature but doesn't look like it. It was weak to this tactic, but we can't do that, well let's go with what we do have and go down the list of things available and see what is the most effective. With the referencing of Lovecraft, specifically Cthulhu, means they had to have seen it and used that piece of fiction as a bases of what to call it and started to compare what it really looked, what it could actually do, and what Cthulhu did in the story to come up with a rational understanding of what and how to deal with it.  When it comes to portrayal, this where more of the deity part needs to be emulated. By that it would need to have more of an effect on the characters psychologically through psychic means. The captain, while having memory issues may be considered an example, the explanation given in this video also partially debunks that notion. Had it been more crew members experiencing something like this, or other weird unexplained events and/or senses being affected. So, for example, strange humming noises or odd high-pitched whines and screeches that seemed more in the head than being heard in the water. Or maybe more hallucination-based stuff like someone seeing something and/or hearing it. While there were moments of something like these, more often than not, it was the creature hunting and probably communicating with others of its kind to ambush the crew much like a pack of wolves. But had comms been more disrupted or there were more unusual noises emanating through the suit comms than just the water this would have been played more in the portrayal aspect and give a bit more solid credence and foundation to yes this is a cosmic horror with powers beyond human comprehension. And if this was the case, then the evolution of underwater apes takes a different approach, and the Cthulhu references still play the used aspect. But now has more fundamental role than just comparison and plays more like the holy grail and the best prophetic writing to take more literally.

regarding the pressure relief valve. Well... that¬¥s a horrible idea. Sure, to us it makes sense. But: decompression sickness is a thing that kills many divers. Gasses dissolve in the tissue, different gasses need to be used for diferent depths etc. So it¬¥s not just a "the suit needs to decrease pressure" thing. Our body literally can¬¥t handle it. N2 in your tissue? you¬¥ll be k.o. and drown. Even oxygen becomes toxic at certain depths. And if you breathe in at 200 atmospheres but your suit decompresses to 50 atmospheres your lung will burst and you will die. So yeah... the suit could have a pressure relief valve. But you would die anyways. So that valve is kinda pointless and would (probably) cause more harm than good. That being said: breathing liquid would be fine. so if the entire suit would¬¥ve been flooded with a liguid that can be used for breathing that would work. but getting that fluid out of your lungs between dives is... challenging.

There was a real life submersible that used glass orbs for buoyancy and was in deep water. It just randomly died and the investigation concluded that 1 orb broke causing the others to. The main differences would be it would implode in like .1 seconds. There would be very little warning.   As for the base, no one would make it. Under water construction is too expansive, and making that base at that depth would be more expensive than colonizing the moon extensively and much less profitable. Legit, any crack any where would be like a water cutter that could take out the whole base. Imagine Titan Gate, but the size of a sky scrapper. It has to be tough because if anything goes wrong, it'd go very wrong too quickly to react. However, if they did build it, it'd be tough enough to withstand those creatures. The water pressure requires it.   Moving on the suits, they look realistic. There was a project to make a deep sea diving suit and it looked really weird, but it was a giant suit of armor. Because of the environment the suit would be a crazy strong and tough bit of kit. The suit would be a match for the monsters we see. The depths would require an extreme outer shell that would be strong enough for the monsters. It'd also have some kind of fighting ability to deal with giant squid; I'm not kidding. The main this in that a space suit costs about $100 mil, so I think these suits would cost $1 Billion or more. There'd only be 1 or 2 suits and they'd be built to last. I think they'd do quite well. Interestingly, they wouldn't suffer from the bends or anything like it because of the rigid exterior so you could get to the surface as fast as you want without exploding issues. It'd be safe.  What's interesting is the creatures. I'm not a biologist, but I have read up on them and deep sea creatures typically have bad cardio. It's cold, there's little food, and little oxygen. This creatures could exist, but they'd be very lethargic or, they'd be anaerobic, meaning they wouldn't use oxygen. Makes sense if they were locked away in a closed pocket of water for some time. If that's the case, O2 would be toxic to them; it's reactive and destructive like acid to these things. They may attack the crew just because they're the only food around. However, these things could have monster strength.   So if this were too happen, I think the crew would be fine, and would probably see it coming. The base would be built like a tank, and could take their attacks. They wouldn't know to hide, and the surveyors would likely find them easily. They'd already have some equipment to deal with the small creatures because of having to fight off giant squids. The big guy would be interesting. Worth noting that the author of the Aquatic Ape Theory heavily regrets calling it that.  It leads to widespread false idea that apes are confirmed to have had an offshoot "return to the water", and become basically mermaids.  That is explicitly *not* what the Aquatic Ape Theory is about.  Rather, the theory relates to how knuckle walking apes transitioned to bipedalism -- by wading in water to forage for food.  While this feat can definitely be achieved by knuckle walking, it is significantly harder for them than a truly bipedal stance would be.

I'm convinced that Underwater is actually the liveaction adaptation of the manga 6000: Rokusen, which was picked up for a liveaction Hollywood movie adaptation in 2015. The manga is about a deep sea research center which was left to rot after an 'incident', and a new batch of people are sent down to start up the research again. Then a series of strange occurrences, sightings, and murders happen; as well as them finding out that the previous researchers had all gotten stuck down in the depths and reverted to ritualistic cannibalism and gone mad, so that when the company actually sent people down there to clean up (not really rescue) them, they were all shot down and killed cos they rushed the mercenaries. It was then found out that in the depths, basically their primal fears had given rise to an actual Aztec god of darkness to manifest, which started to warp the people in it, the entire structure. And it turns out that the ritualistic sacrifices had a 'good' point, because they were to summon the Aztec god of the sun into the depths to push back the darkness god.  So a bunch of researchers get called into a submarine deep sea research facility, where strange things keep happening and there are things in the water. Then a supernatural element is revealed, where an ancient god(s) are shown to be real and being ritualistically summoned. For all the bad in this regarding science and deep water physics. Rodrigo imploding turning into an explosion is actually correct. Have you ever seen an old school CRT Monitor or TV tube get punctured by a bullet or a rock. It's a vacuum in it. So it implodes. So the shattering glass and materials get sucked inwards. But they then go through the center of the implosion and back out the other side at velocity. Unless you have a black hole at the center an implosion becomes in effect an explosion as the force goes through the center and back out.

Not to sound like a huge nerd (though I totally am) with lit, there are two mentions of the beings with Cthulhu. One is in the Call of Cthulhu where it is said none may say whether they all looked like Cthulhu or not. The other is in the Mountains of Madness where they are referred to as the 'spawn of Cthulhu'. One refers to them more like cuttlefish and another reference simply as tentacle headed. This to me always gave me the impression that the beings that Cthulhu has with him aren't exactly what he is. Also in The Mound (which was co written) the human like beings underground say Cthulhu brought them here originally and refer to the original people who arrived as star spawn. So when I saw this movie to me there is Cthulhu of course, but I explain the differences in seemingly two different species as him and then those he brought with him, which I would assume would also undergo some sort of change or evolution being under water this whole time. Edit: Its also important that many of the seemingly supernatural Lovecraftian creatures aren't generally viewed as supernatural by Lovecraft, just as different races from different planets and dimensions that are referred to as gods by humans, but not by Lovecraft himself. He drops little references here and there as to why some of them are able to do things seemingly god like. Most of the supernatural god influences came more from other authors in the mythos.

Hey! Geologist here! I‚Äôm about to go off about oil and Ringwoodite, basically TLDR:  1. We have known about Ringwoodite since 1969 and in 2014 it was confirmed to be in our mantle but the paper that described this believes the water stored there requires an oceanic source to bank water, not that Ringwoodite generates water.  2. Petroleum oil generally only shows up in geologic settings that are directly related to shallow sea environments/shoreline reefs. That‚Äôs how we know it has to come from shallow sea life.    So! The nitty gritty! Ringwoodite was actually originally discovered in 1969 inside the Tenham Meteorite. After its discovery it was theorized to exists in the earth‚Äôs mantle and due to its chemical formula and structure it has the capacity to replace parts of its crystal structure with hydroxide Ions, essentially ionized water, keeping them trapped in its crystal lattice. It was believe it could form in the earth‚Äôs mantle due to the conditions down there being suitable for its formation (that formation requiring the heat and pressure of say a meteorite impact to form. Kick ass.) but that had not been proven until 2014 when a diamond was found with a Ringwoodite inclusion! The diamond had been fired out of the mantle by volcanic eruptions in Brazil , indicating that ringwoodite exists VERY deep in the earth, but the quantities and how much water it could uptake is still uncertain. The paper that suggests the ‚Äú1-3 times the amount of water in our oceans‚Äù hypothesis also suggests that the water got there from billions of years of plate tectonics, with oceanic plates subducting into the earth dragging hydroxide ions deep into the earth to supply the environment with the material to substitute them into Ringwoodite! Basically, it is thought that water was stored there from our seas, not necessarily that it has always been there. It‚Äôs a reservoir of water, not necessarily a source that existed before our oceans. It is part of the water cycle though, and during volcanic eruptions that water is jettisoned back into the atmosphere sort of ‚Äúexhaling‚Äù back out that water into the skies. The earth breaths, and it does so VIOLENTLY.   Also, the oil thing? Simple. Most oil is found in transgressive and regressive series of sandstone, limestone, and shale. These series are almost textbook shoreline environments with the sandstone being analogous to the beach, limestone being analogous to near shoreline coral reefs, and shales being analogous to deeper water muds. As shore lines move backwards when the sea levels rise the series also ‚Äúmoves‚Äù backwards, burring the corals in mud (read shale) and burring the old shoreline in corals (read limestone). When the sea levels fall so too does the series with those corals being covered in sand (sandstone) and those old muds (shale) being grown over by corals (limestone). In the geologic record you can actually see this process going back and forth over and over again in outcrops it is very cool and directly analogous to the formation and retreat of shallow seas on continental crusts or of shoreline growth and retreat on out beaches in the modern day.   But how does that prove oil is formed from sea life? Well petroleum is mainly found in these series, is highly carbon rich (in an environment that without life is fairly carbon bare), and tends to be trapped between the limestone and shale segments, basically the segments where life flourishes and actually makes up the rock itself (limestone) and where life gets buried in a low energy environment (shales).   Hope this clears a few things up!

8:26 üò≥ "OCEANGATED?"  ü§ØüòÑüòÖüòÇü§£üòÜ
The suit implosion would indeed lead to a shock wave, which can be observed in single bubble experiments where a single bubble is initialized at a lower pressure than the ambient pressure. The result, as you would expect, is a very violent implosion that lasts for a fraction of a second. As all the liquid flows into the space previously occupied by the bubble or, in the case of the film, the suit, the "walls" of water collide and create a very powerful shock wave. It's a very interesting effect that is quite well documented in research papers if you want to learn more about it :)

If this movie is based on Lovecraftian stories, like Cthulhu, then the creatures would be Deep Ones, which is even more disturbing when you know the lore. Deep Ones are hybrids between other Lovecraftian monsters and humans, who were sacrificed by coastal tribes in return for good fishing. That mean those sacrificed women had relationship with fish or cephalopods, and then gave birth to these things. There are some stories suggesting that Humans can transform into Deep Ones, but that's more mystical than sci fi and probably doesn't fit with this particular movie.

Metamorphosis/life-stage wise, assuming the leviathan IS the same species, this could be similar to the pond newt. It goes from an aquatic larva (tadpole) that grows legs, loses its fins, and becomes a terrestrial juvenile, and then re-develops fins and other aquatic adaptations when it finally metamorphoses into an aquatic adult. So, there's at least a precedent for an animal with a life cycle that goes from more to less and back to more aquatic-adapted (though losing legs is a stretch).

Thalassaphobia? Boy do I have a story for you fine people!  When I was a child, I lived near the sea. Being a stupid little proto-human, I used to do something with my friends. We'd walk out to this point where the water suddenly gets rather deep. It was sorta like an underwater slop that went down not too far, but a decent distance. We would play a game where, we take our swim goggles, a nose plug, and ear plugs, then drop down the slop and touch the bottom, upon which we swim back up. Sometimes, we'd snag some seaweed, sea trash, or maybe even a crab. The point is, it was fun. Also, on the way up, you'd have this beautiful view of the sunlight pouring down, tinged dark green by the water.  Now, one day, I did my thing (alone, because I was extra stupid that day), went down, touched the bottom, then kicked off the ground to swim back up. I immediately stop because my head bumped into something. I was very confused, so hastily looked up and around to see a shark swimming away. Based solely on guesswork, I bumped this big ol' fish right in the tummy and he just swam off without any trouble. I consider it to be one of my favourite life experiences because I had never seen such a big shark so close, but I figured folks with thalassaphobia might have fun thinking about this one though.

Divers experience psychodelic effects of high preassure gasses at depth (some shit to do with the amount of molecules). Most act as a depressant narcotic, others can act as a stimulant (not sure about stimulant). Helium is the most "innert" at certain depths helium mixtures are neccesery, if going even deeper, you might have to place  different bottles with different mixtures (less oxigen then usual or something) to prevent going too schizo or going ino a deep narcosis, REMEMBER: YOU WILL BE IMPARED at depth, no way to avoid it. A reliefe valve might/or might not be  be a great idea. To explain why. There are 3 different basic  diving gear (not counting going naked) wetsuit, drysuit and aep- athmosperic diving suit.wetsuit is not complicated so no comment.  Drysuit keeps you warm in extremely freezing water by keeping you dry but requires inflation. Basically the deeper you go, the more the drysuit clings to you so you counteract that with inflating it. Go too deep and you cant move (constricted), overinflate (or rise too quickly) and you cant move due to balooning  (and experience the bends) so you can not add/ release preassure to save yourself. Aep keeps 1 atmosphere of preassure, sealed in an exoskeleton with pliers for "hands". These suits seem like a combo of dry and aep. An exoskeleton with weakpoints that are keept from collapsing by additional internal preassure (dont exist currently i think).the internal preassure does not have to match the outside preassure, just reduce its potency (2 atm preassure should halve the required structural integrity, but if someone has better info, please do tell, because im not sure how the difference in preassure works exactly) All in order to reduce the effect of narcosis while maintaining more or less normal mobility. If the valve in the movie suit fails and suit HAS to maintain internal preassure to not collapse.you will run out of oxygen quite fast. Unless the valve was too small to quickly regulate preassure , or has to be manually operated. But why would a suit that can not regulate preassure have such potent  "vertical" thrusters. Also at very deep preassures, regular valve might not work, titanic "excavation" had to use oil or disel for "baloons" because gasses could over compress at some depths for baloons to rise effectively. Rebreathers can fail and cause co2 buildup called co2 hit which will fuck up a diver FAST. And co2  will not clear the bodies system quickly. Rebreathers are used for "practice" , in severe silt or caves where bubbles will impair already limited vision, or to allow a more efficient use of oxigen. The deeper you go the more oxigen you spend on bubbles when you exhale (you breathe out preassurised air which is 10-15%oxigen), rebreather recycles that oxigen by scrubbing c02 and adding a little bit extra air.

My thalassophobia comes from two events: the first being when I went with my dad and brother to the beach in the Outer Banks and my dad was fly fishing at night and, on the back swing, managed to snag a chunk of my neck, and my dad thought it was stuck on the sand or something so he tried yanking to free it, not hearing my terrified screams. He then took out the hook and had me walk about to the rental house by myself, in the dark, bleeding from my neck. I was 10. The second instance was a few years after that when we visited family down in the Florida Keys and my great uncle that we were staying with took us out on his boat to a reef. I'm already nervous because the ground is easily like 30+ feet below me when I jump in, but almost immediately, I become hyperaware of a full sized barracuda just... Watching me. I know in my heart that there's no danger, but when you see THOSE teeth and their owner is just hovering there, menacingly, all that rational thinking goes out the window. Ever since, I don't go further into the ocean than I can comfortably stand because goddamnit, that's where our feet are supposed to be, on the ground, and I am NOT going back into the primordial soup.

The science of an implosion is interesting. Thunder foot did a video about what Happens when a Hull Fails at 1000 atmospheres. In short, water is compressible and when you got a breach the water in that area starts to depress. He explains that if water is compressed you foolishly open the sub's door then you instantly fill when the water depresses to fill the space. So regular pressure water is what get you not the high pressure stuff.

Putting aside my gripes with the dive suits as someone with a scuba diving license, these creatures kinda remind me of Black Swallower  Its a species of deep sea fish that have large expandable stomachs meant to hold prey much larger than itself, which is digested over an extended period of time The Black Swallower is only about 6 to 8 inches, but can eat prey over twice its length and up to 10 times its size  The reason for doing so is that since prey is so scarce it needs to make sure what it catches can last for a long time, and it isnt picky about what it eats It makes me wonder if these creatures having extendable jaws and loose stomach skin, as well as their tendancy to eat things in one go, is because they have similar feeding habits  So the creatures could eat large prey or scavange prey, like whale falls, and then spend long periods digesting it in between hunting for more prey

Unfortunately it's not sea monkeys. The director confirmed the giant monster is Cthulhu, which is really lame.
It's not hypothesized that petroleum came from dinosaurs - that's more of a colloquial misunderstanding. The current theory _(although it is "just a theory" it is backed by a tremendous amount of evidence and disproven by none)_ is that oil n gas come from the slow aneorobic decomposition of mass amounts of single celled bacteria - zooplankton and algae, diatoms - which were cut off from oxygen and then buried under sedimentary rock.  Those decomposition chemicals baking in high pressure for hundreds of millions of years made formed the complex bursting-eith-energy (just add heat) hydrocarbon molecules that make up petroleum.  Coal is essentially the same thing but instead of bacteria it's million-year pressure-baked plants.

Okay, so the way you presented ringwoodite is very misleading. The existence of Ringwood night and the mantle transition zone means there could be as much as three times the amount of surface water trapped inside of the mantle.   Additionally, this was not just recently found out this was very first documented and calculated back in 1969.  Additionally, the water was not " forced into the rocks" this material contains a large amount of hydroxide ions that remains stable at the high pressure and temperature. They would become reactive as they came to the surface over time, but would most likely form large amounts of H2O depending on what other reactants it was around.  Please bear in mind I am not a chemist. My chemistry background stops at organic chemistry, so the part about how it would go from OH to h2o is definitely lacking some knowledge.

So I can respect the stance on Subnautica.   Personally, I find it calming most of the time, but we already know I'm strange.  So now for the science.  I am not an expert, but I can think of 2 reasons why an implosion would cause an outward shockwave.  First, the water imploding in so fast will rebound after the collapse, the same thing happens in reverse during a normal explosion, the shockwave collapses and air rushes back in.  Basically, too much water trying to fill too small of a volume and the rest has to leave.  Secondly, everything in the imploded vessel is now super hot. Boyle's law in action.  The volume of the stuff went down to like 1/10,000th of it's volume with a corresponding increase in temperature.  So now that it's hotter it's actually got more pressure than the water outside for a fraction of a second and it pushes back out.  It could be a bit of both.  It could be something else entirely. Catastrophic implosion in a highly pressurized medium leads to the cavity of lower pressure's volume to decrease rapidly to the point where the air actually has a higher pressure that of the medium. Such rqpid gas state transformations usually are almost adiabatic, which means the gas heats up vigorously to a point where is actually combusts. So yeah, it's like a literal bomb as far as the surroundings of the implosion event are concerned. Basic physics.

19:31. I do work in HSE. And your statement is somewhat correct but missing one theoretical information. In HSE we talk about resilience vs redundancies. Redundancies cost money, nobody wants to spend money so people built more and more resilient systems. This however often entails that those systems are undertstood to be sooo resilient that they don't realy need redundant systems within it. This leads to the resiliance-paradox. Which means if highly resilient system fail - they fail completly and catastrophically.  The best example of that is the banking system, nobody realy thought about a system which may backup the petro-dollar, it was understood to be very resiliant. But it failed, and failed hard. The energy system is the same, there is no real backup to it, if it fails it fails hard so hard that some powerplants could not be turned on again.  The suit might be such a system, where those who buiilt it, within certain constraints, evaluated to to be so resilietn against all known attacks and possible failiures that it doesn't need a back up

8:45 Dude... the crack was not letting pressure out. If it was you would see bubbles. Not only that,but even if it was leaking air out through the crack that would cause a lack of internal suit pressure, which could,itself,cause an implosion. But none of that matters because what happened was,the helmet sustained a serious enough crack that it was no longer structurally sound. So,whether it's an implosion caused by the extreme depth,or an explosion caused by the helmet not being able to withstand its internal pressurization,the result is that the helmet fails structurally.

Just a point, this creature wouldn't be Cthulhu, it would be Dagon, and if you would like a similarly strange film (not sure if you've covered it yet) the titular Dagon is a pretty solid body horror Lovecraftian adaptation.  Also rather than mammalian these creatures could be the end result of primitive aquatic amphibians adapting for the Deep Ocean over moving onto land and forming into mammalian species. The formation of hands and legs could simply be due to a quirk of convergent evolution. Any species living on the ocean floor might find limbs useful for traversing it, and long legs would allow it to perhaps rear upright and simply consume anything it detected in the hunting area (it might very well have been an ambush predator or have some form of non-visual lure).   The larger species also has an arm (one arm and the other is missing, which is perhaps an injury indicating either this species fights over territory or mates, or that there are larger predators or herbivores capable of defending themselves down there), wierdly enough, so it could potentially be some strange offshoot of the same species heading towards gigantism instead of safety in numbers and higher intelligence.

Mostly because we have a finite knowledge of how things work, and unless we gain some knowledge outside of that, we can only really imagine variations of creatures that could exist.  Seeing there are pockets of water, and most likely life, that are sealed off by tectonic events, we would see any emerging creature that didn't fit our knowledge of creatures would instantly seem alien. Given time and study, many of these "alien" creatures we have found within the last 100 years have proven to be well within what we would expect could evolve on this planet. Fun fact, Roanoke, oil is self replacing. üëå   Multiple cases, but one very notable, had an oil well capped in the 70s as a dry well being uncapped and opened again for testing, only to find it had MORE oil inside it than was initially gathered before it was capped as "dry". Implosion can explode.  An implosion can propel material outward (for example due to the force of inward falling material rebounding, or peripheral material being ejected as the inner parts collapse), but this is not an essential component of an implosion and not all kinds of implosion will do so. If the object was previously solid, then implosion usually requires it to take on a more dense form‚Äîin effect to be more concentrated, compressed, or converted into a new material that is denser than the original.

Regarding "implosion causing explosion" - surprisingly yes.  An implosion event causes a flow of water inwards from all sides. And around the centre the waves run into each other and bounce off with huge force. And that creates an outwards going shock wave that under right conditions can be more powerful than an implosion.  The most spectacular example of this process is super nova. But underwater this also pretty easy to notice if you for example watch a slow motion footage of bullet travelling through water.

A future movie recommendation: Alligator from 1980.  At first it is just another cash in of the killer animal craze from Jaws.  However unlike a lot of movies that just role with "Wow, how can this animal be so big?" there is an in movie explanation involving growth hormones.  Illegal tests on dogs and other animals where used to see if they could make them grow twice the size.  However when they where done they dropped the bodies into the sewers and guess what just happened to be living in those sewers and ate the dead dogs?  Really might make for a fun episode down the line.  Also it's currently on Shudder so it's easy to find.
